Lin Xigui Appointed as Principal of the Mawei Naval Academy 113

Negotiations on the Scope of Authority are Currently Underway

Inspection Report to be Printed Soon

Admiral Du Xigui was ordered by the National Government to go to Europe, America, and Japan to inspect naval construction. After returning to China last autumn, he immediately began to organize his inspection report. Naval Minister Yang Shuzhuang recently obtained his consent and plans to appoint Du as the principal of the Mawei Naval Academy. Yesterday, this reporter interviewed Du at his private residence to inquire about the date of his assumption of office and future reorganization plans. According to Du, the Mawei Naval Academy has always been under the jurisdiction of the Naval Department, and all matters must be submitted to the Naval Department for handling. He is currently discussing the issue of the principal's authority with Minister Yang and Vice Minister Chen. If he can be given full authority without being restricted by the Naval Department, then he may be able to take on the position. Therefore, this matter is still under discussion. The Mawei Naval Academy is a specialized school, and students are sent by various provinces and recommended by naval officers' children. The scale is still large. In the future, after the Xiangshan military port is built, it may be moved there, which will make it easier to expand. The reporter also inquired whether the inspection report on the navies of various countries had been printed. He replied that the entire report is divided into twelve volumes and is still being printed. He is personally responsible for proofreading, and it will be published in about a month. A total of one thousand copies will be printed, which will be distributed to various agencies at that time.

Naval Torpedo Fleet Returns to Shanghai After Exercises in Xiangshan Port 114

The naval torpedo fleet, led by Commander Zeng Yiding, sailed to Xiangshan military port for exercises, firing torpedoes, practicing formations, and combat maneuvers for nearly a week. It was not until the day before yesterday that the exercises were completed. Commander Zeng immediately boarded the flagship Yongjian and led the team back to Shanghai, arriving at the Songkou port at about 3:30 PM yesterday. The flagship Yongjian led the way, followed by seven torpedo boats: Hupeng, Huzhun, Huzi, Chenzi, Suzi, Liezi, and Zhangzi, one after another, heading straight for Shanghai. When entering the port, the Wusong Fortress Naval Command and the National Coast Guard both raised flags and fired salutes to pay their respects. The torpedo fleet also returned the salute in accordance with the protocol. At about 6:00 PM, they sailed to Shanghai and are now gathered at the Gaoyangmiao port.

This order."

Li Jingcong Discusses Details of the Eurasian Aircraft Being Shot Down 122

The Number One Aircraft was also Damaged by Mongolian Soldiers

The Company is Negotiating for Rescue

Regarding the shooting down of the Number Two aircraft of the Eurasian Aviation Corporation on its northbound journey on the 2nd by foreign Mongolian troops, yesterday's newspaper had a brief report. A reporter from the Daily News visited Mr. Li Jingcong, the director of the company's operations group, again yesterday. According to Mr. Li, in addition to the damaged aircraft that was shot down, the Number One aircraft that went to investigate and rescue reported that it was also shot and injured. A rescue plan has now been discussed. The details are as follows:

Continuing Telegrams Received Yesterday 123

The company received a continuing telegram yesterday from Jiang Da, director of the Manchurian branch office, and Liu Zhi, the pilot of Eurasian aircraft Number One, stating that while passing through the southeastern corner of Lake Buir, they saw with a telescope that Eurasian aircraft Number Two was parked on the east side of a nearby Mongolian village, with the fuselage intact, but the traces of the pilots Lai Qi and others had not been found. They also said that when they went to investigate on the 6th, they intended to land to inquire about the situation, but suddenly heard gunshots near the ground, violently shooting at the fuselage. As a result, they dared not stop and urgently flew to Manzhouli. After arriving at the Manzhouli airfield and inspecting the aircraft, they learned that the wings and fuel tanks were severely damaged. They immediately ordered a quick repair, and the aircraft left Manzhouli early this morning, taking the route through Linxi, and is expected to fly back to Peiping around noon today. Lake Buir is located about 240 kilometers south of Manzhouli and is under the jurisdiction of Hailar in this province. The southeastern side of the lake is the border between Hailar and Outer Mongolia. Since Outer Mongolia unilaterally declared independence, it seems that troops have been stationed in the area.

Reason for Crossing the Border 124

Mr. Li also told the reporter from the Daily News that the reason for the Number Three aircraft's mistaken entry into Outer Mongolia, in addition to what was reported in yesterday's newspaper, also had the following reasons. According to my (Mr. Li's self-proclaimed) speculation, the reasons are probably no more than the following: (1) Because the border area is very close to the route taken by the aircraft, it is easy to cross the border inadvertently. As for the reason for landing there, it must have been caused by being subjected to strong gunfire when it mistakenly entered the area.

Post-Accident Measures 125

Currently, Director Jiang of the company's Manzhouli office has dispatched two people familiar with the situation in Outer Mongolia to investigate the message that the aircraft was seized, along with news of the aircraft fuel tank engine and more, if there were any injuries. Also, because Outer Mongolia and Soviet Russia have good relations, he asked the Soviet Consul stationed in Manzhouli to find a way to negotiate and rescue the seized. It is hoped that the company's aircraft is of postal transport nature. They also have no military purpose. Because both trips to and from their flight have been for about two months, there is no intentional entry into the Outer Mongolian region that can be released. For safety reasons, is the company's aircraft still intended to take the straight flight between Linxi and Manzhouli after the misunderstanding has not been cleared and a solution has not been reached, and should the company evaluate and consult on this matter.

Advice from British Women's Leaders on China's Anti-Opium Campaign 134

The Disguised Public Opium Trade is Inferior to the Qing Dynasty

Opium Taxation Violates the Treaty

The Chinese National Anti-Opium Society has received hundreds of letters and telegrams from local party branches, anti-drug organizations, and mass organizations in recent days, expressing unanimous protests against the implementation of the disguised opium public sale by the Anti-Opium Prohibition and Investigation Office. It is reported that the Society received telegrams yesterday from American anti-drug leaders, Ms. Raymond, Mrs. Fred, and Mrs. Wright, expressing regret over the central government's anti-opium policy and urging the Chinese National Anti-Opium Society to actively protest and submit their true intentions to the State Council for adoption. Ms. Raymond is a well-known leader in the anti-drug movement with numerous works and a worldwide reputation. Mrs. Fred's new anti-drug novel (Conseceme) is praised by European and American opinion as the best work of humanitarian merit since Uncle Tom's Cabin. It has now been translated into Chinese by the Chinese National Anti-Opium Society under the name "Black Sea Retribution" and will be published soon. As for Mrs. Wright, she is the former director of the League of Nations' anti-opium division and the leader of the American delegation to the International Anti-Opium Conference, who recently toured the Far East and China. Her comments have always been valued by the world, and her claims are sufficient to influence the attitude of European and American opinion. Chinese people should be vigilant about such advice. It is reported that the American National Women's Alliance has also convened a meeting on this matter and will submit a protest soon. The translated version of Ms. Raymond's and others' opinions is as follows: (1) It is heard that the Chinese government is now establishing an opium public trade agency to manage and sell opium and to collect taxes from it to enrich the national treasury. (2) The result of spreading this news has greatly affected the opinion of all circles in the United States, which is most unfortunate. Under imperial rule, China was able to actively struggle to eradicate the planting of poppies, but the current National Government cannot exert the same force to protect the lives and happiness of the people. Is it not as good as a tyrannical government? The entire American people are deeply horrified. This kind of plan that is sufficient to diminish the prestige of the Chinese government in the international community is something that even the friendly nations of China believe is absolutely unacceptable. Moreover, the establishment of an opium public trade agency violates the 1912 Hague Opium Convention. The United States actively participated in this convention for the benefit of China.

Page 14

(3) No friend of China is better than Bishop Brent. At the 1924 International Anti-Opium Conference, Bishop Brent expressed the view that the greatest event for us to help China is to lead the Chinese government to resist all temptations to establish an opium public trade agency. Some say that if we do not use this evil trade to collect huge profits, others will also take it. Or they think that a country that uses the exploitation of human weaknesses and sins as a source of revenue can become a glorious government. This flippant view is deeply distressing. (4) The argument that the establishment of opium public sales is a temporary expediency is theoretically unsound. There is no precedent for the cancellation of any public sale that has been established. (5) We hereby request your society to submit this matter to your country's State Council. (6) We hereby request that the State Council strictly enforce the anti-opium ban based on the following two principles: (A) Please use the spirit of an independent country to strictly prohibit the planting, transportation, trafficking, and smoking of opium in China. Move forward bravely without worrying about the obstacles of extraterritoriality and unequal treaties. (B) Please absolutely prohibit the implementation of national, provincial, county, town, and opium public sales or disguised public sales.

News from the Opium Suppression and Investigation Bureau 135

The National Opium Prohibition Committee, based on resolutions from the National Assembly and the Fifth Plenary Session, regarding phased prohibition methods, and in accordance with Article 11 of the Implementing Rules for Opium Prohibition, has established Opium Suppression and Investigation Bureaus in each province, specifically responsible for investigating and suppressing the import, smuggling, and private consumption of opium and various substitute narcotics, in order to gradually achieve the goal of eradication. The director of the bureau for this province and Shanghai Municipality has already been appointed by the Opium Prohibition Committee to Mr. Feng Wenyu, as previously reported in this newspaper. Director Feng has a deep revolutionary history, having served as the director of salt affairs anti-smuggling bureaus in Fujian, Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Anhui, and other provinces, where he earned a good reputation. After being appointed this time, he immediately established the investigation bureau at Xieqiao in this city, urging officials to work diligently. In recent days, they have cracked down on a significant number of cases involving the smuggling and concealment of opium and red pills. At important ports in other regions, water and land investigation posts have been established in accordance with regulations, specifically responsible for investigation and anti-smuggling duties. No specialized investigation commissioners have been established in each county. It is also heard that the bureau, in order to eliminate the poisonous atmosphere, intends to establish a smoking cessation hospital. Rumors outside about merchants contracting for sales, after multiple investigations, are known to be just rumors and not factual.

Merger of Stock Sections of the Exchange Considered Yesterday 136

Differences of opinion remain

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Ministries of Industry and Finance, considering that the prices of various bonds traded at the Shanghai Securities and Goods Exchange and the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange sometimes vary, and in order to maintain the stability of the bond market and reassure people, should merge the securities sections of the two exchanges ahead of schedule, and merge them into the Chinese Merchants Exchange within two months. Securities Held a Board Meeting Yesterday 137

After receiving instructions from the Ministries of Finance and Industry on the fourth of this month, the Securities and Goods Exchange immediately notified all directors to hold a board meeting at the exchange yesterday afternoon. All directors attended, chaired by Chairman Yu Qiaqing.

As a result of the discussion, the exchange supervisors Chen Xing and Xu Jianping scheduled a representative meeting at the supervisor's office at 5:00 PM yesterday, and Yu was appointed as the authorized representative to attend this meeting. The meeting adjourned.

Yesterday afternoon, the Shanghai Exchange representative meeting was attended by securities representative Yu Qiaqing, Chinese Merchants representative Zhang Weiru, and the two supervisors Chen and Xu. Merger Problem Still Needs Time 139

Yesterday, the reporter inquired about opinions from various parties on this matter. Important Shipping News

Agreement on Deck Tax 146

The Jianghai Customs' collection of deck cargo tax from merchant ships has been unanimously opposed by Shanghai shipping merchants, who have petitioned the ministry for exemption. The ministry approved that they should consult with the Commissioner of Customs. Shipping bureaus held another meeting to discuss this matter. Since the Customs is determined to collect tax on deck cargo, there must be restrictions to avoid suffering for the shipping industry. The representatives agreed and elected Yu Qiaqing and Yuan Lüdeng, along with He Molin, Deputy Chief of Business of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, to go to the Customs to negotiate a fixed principle for the collection of deck tax per ton. Moreover, the shipping merchants proposed that deck tax be paid only by ships on the (1) Yangtze River line, (2) Shanghai-Ningbo line, (3) Tongyang line, (4) Shanghai-Taiwan line, (5) Shanghai-Shasha line, and (6) Shanghai-Chongming line. Ships on other ocean routes will not pay. The tax rate will be one fen of silver per ton as determined by the Customs. The three representatives still need to discuss with the Commissioner of Customs.

Opposition to Registration Fee 147

After the establishment of the Maritime Affairs Administration, according to Article 62 of the Ship Registration Law, merchant ships should pay a registration fee. Shipping bureaus have held multiple meetings on this matter and have petitioned the ministry for exemption. Now, they have put forward a resolution: Chinese merchant ships have all been registered with the Ministry of Communications and issued certificates, and the customs have registered and issued licenses. If the Maritime Affairs Administration orders the payment of huge registration fees again, it would be redundant and the government orders would be repetitive, which would be too much to bear. In addition to requesting the Ministry of Communications to approve free registration for all ships that have already been registered and licensed with the Ministry and registered and licensed with the Customs to alleviate the difficulties of merchants, each shipping bureau will respectfully report to the Maritime Affairs Administration for registration, but will not pay fees and will eliminate redundancy.

Normal Exports Today 148

Today is the anniversary of the National Revolutionary Army's Northern Expedition. The Jianghai Customs will also be closed for one day. All export goods from Shanghai-Ningbo, Yangtze River, Shanghai-Taiwan, and North-South Ocean ships that should have been exported today were all declared and loaded in advance yesterday and customs duties were paid. Therefore, they will still be loaded and departed as usual.

Sanmen Bay Investigation Group Scheduled to Depart 149

This matter is a precursor to the people's development of industry, and the government's increased maintenance shows its promotional efforts. Resolution of Labor Dispute at Ruirong Iron Factory 152

All Hourly Workers Given Severance Pay and Dismissed

According to Xinsheng News Agency, the Ruirong Iron Factory on Yangshupu Road, due to business reasons, starting in June, transferred 48 workers, including Chen Qingsheng, to work in shifts, working three days a week. All the workers believed that this was proposed by the foreman Zhang Wende, so they clashed with the foreman, resulting in Zhang being injured. The foreman Smith dismissed all the hourly workers. The labor union sent personnel to negotiate, but with no results. They petitioned the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs for assistance. The bureau sent personnel to mediate twice. The labor side demanded reinstatement, otherwise, they would receive severance pay equivalent to twelve weeks' wages, like the regular workers. The employer insisted on not reinstating them and only agreed to give each person severance pay for twelve days. Therefore, it has been more than a month now and it is still impossible to resolve the matter. The workers went to the authorities to petition the day before yesterday. In order to avoid escalating the labor dispute, the bureau convened a labor-management mediation meeting again yesterday afternoon. The factory foreman Smith and worker representatives Du Zhongwen and Chen Qingsheng, Chairman Gu Bingyuan, and recorder Jiang Shifu attended. The two sides argued fiercely. After repeated persuasion by the chairman, a resolution was reached and a contract was signed as follows: (1) The employment relationship between the 48 hourly workers, including Du Zhongwen and Chen Qingsheng, and the Ruirong Iron Factory is terminated. (2) The factory will give each worker six weeks' wages as severance pay.

Extremely Severe Disaster Situation in Henan 153

The Chinese Red Cross Society recently received a telegram from Commissioner Li Huanying of the Henan Provincial Disaster Relief Committee: "Respectful greetings to Mr. Wang Peiyuan of the Chinese Red Cross Society. Tanghe is unfortunate, having suffered repeated disasters. Since the founding of the Republic, the city has been broken eight times, and the people have suffered terribly. The vitality has not yet recovered. In the past three years, it has been broken once a year. Last year, the Communists occupied the city, burning, killing, and looting, which was already extremely cruel. Unexpectedly, before they could catch their breath, at dawn on May 30, the city was captured by the giant bandit Cui Erdan. It was found that the bandit occupied the city for twenty days, sending teams out every day to attack towns and loot villages, arbitrarily kidnapping. Within fifty miles around, the residents fled. There is no one. It is the time when the two wheats are ripe.

Scorched on the ground, no one to harvest. According to refugees who escaped and people from Huanying's family who came to Bian to report, they wept uncontrollably and said: "Two or three thousand people were killed in the city, and more than ten thousand were dragged away. Eighty or ninety percent of the houses were destroyed. Even worse, women were forced to be raped, and children were thrown to their deaths. The bandits gathered to watch and took it as pleasure. They also took advantage of the two wheats being scorched to set fire and burn, extending to the fields and wilds to celebrate. All kinds of tragic situations are unbearable to describe. It is truly an unprecedented catastrophe. Huanying is a fellow villager and feels the pain deeply. He longs for his hometown, but cannot return. The livelihood of hundreds of thousands of victims is currently hopeless, and the autumn harvest in the future is uncertain. Cries of starvation are everywhere. I respectfully appeal, and sincerely hope that you will be mindful of the enormity of the bandit disaster in Tanghe this time, and devise special methods to raise a large sum of disaster relief funds and immediately provide relief. The 300,000 lives in the county will all feel your great kindness forever. I send this urgent telegram with a hundred bows, without appointment, and earnestly pray." Li Huanying of the Henan Provincial Disaster Relief Committee, gratefully kowtowing.

Appeal for Flood Relief in Jiangxi 155

The Chinese and Foreign Relief Committee received a telegram from the New Construction Flood Relief Aftermath Committee yesterday: "Jiangxi is in a state of devastation. Bandit disasters have not subsided, and flood disasters have been added. It is early summer, and the massive floods are overwhelming. Hurricanes have taken advantage of this to collapse embankments and uproot houses. Fields and gardens are flooded, and families are displaced. Every household has suffered. The situation is extremely tragic. The province has already sent telegrams, which you are presumed to be aware of. However, our New Construction County is located in the middle of the Gan River and is close to the western Wen of Poyang Lake. The terrain is low-lying and the disaster is particularly severe. In the past, the upstream water burst and many embankments collapsed. Afterwards, the downstream water suddenly rose, and the accumulation has no way to dissipate. Now, it has been more than two months, and the river water is a vast expanse. The people are sick and dying, which is heartbreaking to see. The early rice sowing has already been delayed, and the late rice harvest will be hopeless. In a county that is known for its poverty, and in the face of this extraordinarily tragic disaster, alas, the people, how can we save the dead? This is why we must hope that the charitable people of the world will show special pity." It is heard that the Chinese and Foreign Relief Committee has already prepared 10,000 yuan to help with emergency relief. However, the summer days are long, the disaster area is expanding, and there are cries of starvation everywhere. Without a large sum of disaster relief funds, how can we help? We earnestly hope that all sectors of society will show great compassion and actively provide relief.

Rice Boat Capsized, Crew Drowned 156

Three Dead

The rice boat Tao Kangting recently collected more than 190 shih of white rice from farmers in Zhangjin area of Songjiang and transported it to Shanghai for sale. On the morning of the sixth, before dawn, there was heavy rain and a very rough sea. Tao's boat anchored by the Dujia Hang riverbank in Nanhuangpu. Tao and his crew were all fast asleep. Unexpectedly, the rain was even heavier and the waves were even more violent. The iron anchor chain broke and the boat was washed away by the waves. The iron feet on board were very heavy, and the rainwater inside the boat made it even heavier. Suddenly, a gust of wind and waves caused the whole boat to sink. Tao and his crew were all asleep at the time. They were startled by the water flooding the cabin. The boat was gradually sinking. Tao and one of the crew rushed out of the cabin, their bodies already wet. The other three crew members did not have time to climb out and drowned in the boat. In a hurry, Tao threw a cabin plank into the river, clung to it, and drifted to Luya, where he was rescued by a cargo ship. One of Tao's crew members grabbed onto the main mast and called for help. Later, he was rescued by a small boat from Jiangbei. Yesterday, he hired a boat to go to the scene of the accident. When the tide receded, they saw the boat exposed above the water. They hired craftsmen to go down into the cabin and tie up the three crew members who had drowned and lift them up. They moved the corpses to the shore for purchase of coffins and burial. Now, they are hiring machinery to try to salvage the boat, but it will cost a lot. Tao is very frustrated because all his belongings were on the boat and he suffered this misfortune.

A Destitute Man Found on the Bund Grass 157

Died from Poisoning

Hua Bu No. 1172 of the Fourth Road General Patrol Room was patrolling the Bund area at 6:00 AM yesterday when he saw a destitute man, estimated to be about 30 years old, lying on the grass. He was wearing a black cotton-padded jacket and white cotton trousers. He looked abnormal and haggard. He was immediately sent to Renji Hospital. After examination by a doctor, it was discovered that he had ingested alcohol and poison. Although they tried their best to give him injections and medicine, it was of no use. He died at around 9:00 PM that evening. The body was transferred from the hospital to the morgue for examination by the court.

The heavy rain in the past two days has caused damage. Many dilapidated houses in this city have collapsed. With a crash, the thatched house collapsed. Zhou escaped, but Zhou's wife, who was over sixty years old, was crushed inside. Her skin was broken and her bones were fractured. Two Floating Corpses, Male and Female

Male Corpse at Dongjiadu 162

At around 7:00 AM yesterday, Feng Dengan, a watchman policeman of the 16th post of the 1st precinct of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, found an unidentified male corpse resembling a boatman on the Dongjiadu wharf in the southern city. He was about 20 years old, wearing a blue cloth short shirt, black cloth trousers, barefoot, without shoes or socks, and his hair was cut in a flat-top style. He immediately reported the situation to the station chief. Considering that it involved human life, he immediately ordered Qin Defang, the local chief of the 23rd ward, to report to the Shanghai Local Court and request an autopsy. At around 2:00 PM, Prosecutor Wu, commissioned by the court, and the coroner arrived at the scene to conduct an autopsy. It was found that the skin on the waist of the corpse was bruised. It was determined that he had been beaten before his death due to injuries. He ordered the local chief to report to the hall to provide a coffin and store the body in a shrine, waiting for the corpse's relatives to identify and claim it.

Bagao Advertising Company Undergoes Major Reorganization 167

Working Together with Rickshaw Companies

Bagao Advertising Company, located at 36 Renji Road, pioneered advertising on rickshaw hoods, creating a unique and novel approach that caused quite a sensation in Shanghai. It was hailed as one of the most innovative developments in the advertising industry. However, due to its initial rudimentary nature, it was not perfect. Subsequently, it underwent repeated reforms, consuming countless efforts and financial resources. It was changed to sheet metal advertisements, resembling miniature versions of street signs in the market, printed with colorful oil paints, beautiful, bright, and exceptionally eye-catching. However, the costs were too high, and the procedures were cumbersome, making it uneconomical for advertising clients. Now, to facilitate client advertising and reduce their burden, it has been changed to multi-colored finely printed posters pasted on the sheet metal. Its effectiveness far surpasses that of advertisements on trams and public buses. Rickshaws travel to every corner of the city, reaching all social classes, who enjoy using them for transportation. The advertisements on their hoods are constantly in view, deeply imprinted in people's minds. Moreover, the cost can be reduced by half, and advertising rates are also particularly low. Those interested in placing such advertisements are requested to call 12919 to inquire about prices and learn everything. Yesterday, several vehicles had already pasted these advertisements, and those who saw them were quite amazed, believing that rickshaw advertising, after its reforms, has reached a flawless stage, attracting exceptional attention.

Further Hearing on the Riyue Bank Debt Case 177

Da Shijie Placed with Huang Jinrong

Investigating a Jadeite Worth 100,000 Yuan

Two Accountants Request Payment of Public Expenses

Huang's Family Members Request Living Expenses

Shanghai Riyue Bank and Da Shijie Amusement Deposit Department declared bankruptcy after the death of Huang Chu Jiu. The French Concession Court repeatedly summoned witnesses and engaged accountants Pan Zhaobang and Wu Cheng to liquidate the assets and distribute one-tenth of the recovered funds to creditors. These events have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, the French Concession Court summoned witnesses again. Accountant Pan Zhaobang stated that an agreement had been reached with Mr. Huang Jinrong regarding the sale of Da Shijie for 700,000 yuan. A contract had been signed and submitted for review. The payment is expected to be made around the end of July. Furthermore, Mr. Huang acknowledged and agreed to pay the monthly rent of 10,000 yuan for July in full. In addition, the accountants discovered during the inventory of Huang Chu Jiu's estate that Huang Chu Jiu possessed a jadeite worth 100,000 yuan, weighing 320 jin, which was entrusted to Liu Baogeng for washing and cutting. Liu has now been brought to court and is requested to hand it over. Liu Baogeng, represented by lawyer Lin Yingqing, stated that in April or May of last year, Huang Chu Jiu purchased two jadeite stones from Yunnan merchant Chen Kaiqing, totaling 600 jin, one weighing 280 jin and one weighing 320 jin, for 30,000 yuan. The 320-jin jadeite was discussed with Liu Baogeng, who was to transport it to Beiping for washing and cutting, with the condition that Liu would contribute 30% of the shares and be responsible for paying the processing fees. Future profits would be evenly distributed. At that time, Liu Baogeng consulted with colleagues Ma Yurong and Lu Junren, who deemed the goods reliable. An agreement was reached, and they successively paid 4,800 yuan, of which 3,900 yuan was paid with three checks from Riyue Bank, and 900 yuan was paid in cash. Yizhengrong Jade Workshop is currently washing and cutting the jadeite. All of this can be verified with the original goods, handling personnel, and accounts. It is actually co-owned by Liu Baogeng and Huang Chu Jiu and cannot be considered Huang's private property. This is the true situation. Subsequently, creditor representatives Yan Luqing and Bian Jialu, both lawyers, stated that according to Liu Baogeng's representative lawyer, Liu also has a 30% interest in the jadeite and must provide concrete evidence, otherwise, they deny it. They requested that Liu Baogeng be required to provide 100,000 yuan in silver and security and be given a deadline to hand over the jadeite. Liu's representative lawyer, Lin Yingqing, stated that all of Liu Baogeng's statements are true. Check stubs are available for verification. If Liu Baogeng were not honest, he could simply deny everything. Moreover, Liu has substantial property in the jurisdiction and does not need to provide security. The court ordered the jadeite to be handed over to the court within 21 days. Furthermore, lawyer Peng Qi stated that his lawyer represents Wanchun Silver Group and that all public expenses should be calculated at 3%, totaling 9,000 yuan. His lawyer is now offering a reduction to 4,500 yuan and requests that it be allocated from Huang's estate. The court ruled to allocate 3,000 yuan and allow it to be deducted from Huang's estate. Accountants Pan Zhaobang and Wu Cheng stated that they also request that all public expenses be assessed according to the public association's regulations. Lawyer Dong Yu stated that regarding the public expenses requested by Pan and Wu, they have worked hard since taking over the liquidation and their request for public expenses is appropriate. His lawyer does not object. The court ruled to wait for further review. It is heard that Huang's family members are requesting living expenses. Their representative lawyer, Tan Yigong, has sent a letter to all creditors, scheduling a meeting today to discuss the matter.

Kidnapping or Compensation? 178

For a Mere 16 Yuan?

Criminals Would Not Likely Open Fire

Calling It Kidnapping Seems Unlikely

At 9:40 PM last night, a confusing incident that resembled but was not quite a kidnapping occurred at number 100, Caishi Road, in the French Concession. The criminals even opened fire to resist arrest. The details are as follows:

Recent Relocation 179

Two days ago, Futai Paint Shop, located near the Caishi Market at number 100, Caishi Road in the French Concession, rented out a vacant three-story building. A Taizhou man named Wang Hezheng rented the building and moved in with his family. Besides Wang himself, the family includes Wang's wife, Ms. Bao, his mother-in-law, his brothers-in-law Guangde and Guangrong, Wang's eldest son Gonghan, and his second daughter Heyu, totaling seven people.

Screaming Kidnapping 180

Around 9:30 PM last night, four burly men suddenly arrived, went straight to the third floor of number 100, and entered the Wang family's room. At that time, Wang had just returned home. Upon seeing Wang inside, the men immediately showed anger and ordered Wang to come downstairs. Wang, seeing the unfavorable situation, immediately refused. The men did not allow any explanation and forcibly dragged Wang downstairs and escorted him away. Wang's family immediately leaned over the railing and screamed "Kidnapping!"

Second Outcry 181

At that time, Hua Constable Liu Delin from Shandong, number 630, was on duty near the Caishi Market. He heard the alarm and rushed to investigate. The screams quickly subsided. The constable saw no one reporting and immediately returned to his post. At the same time, a Vietnamese constable from Sandao Tou passed by on patrol and asked the constable to sign the logbook. No sooner had he finished signing than the cry for help arose again.

Both Sides Open Fire 182

Upon hearing this, Constable Liu returned and saw an old woman holding onto a man, claiming that the man was a lookout for the criminals. When the man saw the constable approaching, he suddenly broke free, sprinted towards the alley entrance across the street, and fled. Constable Liu pursued him. Just as he entered the alley, a gunshot was heard. Constable Liu also drew his gun and fired. As he rounded the corner, another shot was fired, and a pellet hit the ground, covering Constable Liu's face with dust.

Taken to a Teahouse 183

Seeing two shots in rapid succession, Constable Liu also fired three shots in return. Unfortunately, the fourth bullet was stuck inside the chamber and could not fire, so he did not dare to pursue further and returned to report to the police station. The police chief immediately dispatched detectives Mao Jingen and others to investigate. However, Wang Hezheng was nowhere to be found. At the same time, a passerby secretly reported that the criminals had taken Wang to Tianle Teahouse at number 138, Tiantai Road. Detective Mao immediately led the detectives to surround and capture them.

Debt Dispute 184

Upon arriving at Tianle Teahouse, the hall was empty. He inquired with the owner of the teahouse, who stated that a moment ago, three or five people had brought a man from Taizhou to drink tea. He vaguely heard that the Taizhou man owed someone 16 yuan and had not paid it for a long time. Tonight, they had gathered a group of people to seek revenge, leading to the misunderstanding of a kidnapping. However, until late at night, Wang Hezheng was still nowhere to be found. Moreover, if it was truly to collect a mere 16 yuan, it was absolutely unnecessary to gather a gang, carry weapons, and open fire to resist arrest. If it was truly a kidnapping, why bring Wang to a teahouse? It is truly perplexing. The police station has ordered detectives to thoroughly investigate and uncover the truth.

Discussion on the Shanghai Datong Music Society's Invention of New Musical Notation 191

After the Shanghai Datong Music Society completed the manufacture of 163 ancient and modern, elegant and popular musical instruments (now housed at the World College), Zheng Jinwen, the director of the society, personally tested each instrument and found them to have considerable value. These musical instruments are divided into 13 major categories: metal, stone, silk, bamboo, gourd, earth, leather, wood, clay flute, reed pipe, leather, horsehair, and shell. They have natural scales, four-tone scales, seven-tone scales, nine-palace scales, twelve-tone scales, sixteen-character scales, and small-one-tone (i.e., 24-tone) scales, totaling eight types. Now, to carry out the second step of work, it is truly necessary to create new notation. After five months of examination, the old gongche notation and other notations were found to be inapplicable. Therefore, the five-line staff has been expanded to a seven-line staff, changing the seven-tone nature to a twelve-tone nature. Short lines are added above and below the center line of the high and low sections (a total of three lines). The second line is used as the tonic, totaling seven used notes and five rest notes as one step. If a line is used, the space is a rest; if a space is used, the line is a rest. The key signature only needs to draw an S between the third and fourth used notes for identification. All keys can be inferred from this, which can save a lot of trouble with sharp and flat signs. Chinese music emphasizes fingering the most. The old notation details the fingering and neglects the rhythm. The five-line staff details the rhythm but is difficult to fill in the fingering. However, the seven-line staff method can compensate for both. Furthermore, by distinguishing the shape of the notes with squares, circles, large, and small sizes, the live, fixed, light, and heavy aspects of the music can be expressed. Thus, any music can be recorded without omission. Mr. Zheng has already compiled a zither score and a pipa score using this method and handed them over to the core members of the society, such as Liu Wei and others, for thorough study to achieve perfection. In the future, they will be printed into a volume for musicians around the world to adopt.

Banning the Performance of Plays Based on the Zhujing Murder Case 192

Recently, since the Zhujing Wang family murder case occurred, various institutions and entertainment venues in this city have been competing to opportunistically stage plays based on the case. The Education Bureau of this city believes that this case is related to public morals, and performing it on various stages is tantamount to promoting lewdness and murder, which has a significant impact. The Tianchan Stage, Guang Stage, Small World, Tianyun Building, Xinxin Amusement Park, and several other theaters that have adapted and performed plays based on the case have been severely ordered to stop performing, and notices have been sent to various newspapers to remove all advertisements related to the plays.

Unresolved Case of the Nisshin Masaru Ramming a Shaoxing Junk 193

The case of the Nisshin Masaru, belonging to the Dalian Branch of the Nisshin Company, violently sinking the Shaoxing junk Xu Huiyuan, loaded with glass, at Renjiagang Port in Nantong on April 10th, has been under negotiation for over two months. After receiving the petition from the victim Xu Huiyuan, the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, in addition to forwarding it as appropriate, immediately replied in a letter stating: "Regarding the Xu Huiyuan junk sunk by the Nisshin Masaru, a black-hulled steamship of the Dalian Steamship Company, we received your association's telegram and immediately submitted it to the Ministry for handling, and also replied accordingly. Appendix Evidence 196

Because the Nisshin Masaru wanted to return to Shanghai after unloading coal at Tianshenggang, the responsibility and how to resolve it in the future will be negotiated after both parties arrive in Shanghai." Signed by Captain Yoshida Sadao of the Nisshin Masaru, River Pilot Li Guangyin, Representative Xu Gang of the Zhejiang Shipping Association, and Inspector Long Yuhang of the Renjiagang Water Police. Case of Forging the Ju'an Sugar Company Seal 197

Complex Case

Summoning Records for Re-Examination

Zhang Songzhou, a comprador from Guangdong at the Datong Bank on Jiangxi Road, was recently accused of forgery in the Special District Court by Guo Shuopeng, the owner of the Ju'an Sugar Company on Yangxing Street in the French Concession. The plaintiff's complaint states: "The plaintiff has never guaranteed any monetary debts for anyone. Suddenly, on February 9th of the 17th year of the Republic of China, the plaintiff received a letter from Datong Bank stating that the Ju'an Company, which the plaintiff established, had guaranteed eight batches of foreign exchange advances for the Tongde Company. Hearing this, the plaintiff was extremely surprised and immediately asked a friend, Chen Weiqing, to inquire. He saw ten orders bearing the wooden chop of Guo Ju'an. At that time, the wooden chop did not have any words indicating responsibility. On March 13th, the plaintiff asked lawyer He Shimai to accompany his friend Weng Huidong to inquire at the bank. The bank manager presented a large order but only allowed lawyer He to view it from a distance. Lawyer He immediately denied it on the spot. On March 18th, Datong commissioned lawyer Xu Li to send a letter, demanding that the plaintiff assume responsibility and claiming 20,000 taels. On April 4th, the plaintiff asked a lawyer to reply, denying the guarantee. On June 15th, the plaintiff sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce, requesting that it be forwarded to Zhang Songzhou, a comprador at Datong Bank, to quickly bring the forged order to the General Chamber of Commerce to verify who forged it for prosecution purposes. Zhang Songzhou replied to the Chamber of Commerce, stating that he intended to file a lawsuit with the court and could not bring it. The plaintiff waited quietly for Datong to file a lawsuit, but it did not proceed for a year. In the middle, Mr. Ke Wendi, a foreign manager from the Mei Yong Petroleum Company, sent a letter, urging the plaintiff to reconcile with Datong, otherwise, he would testify in court, proving that the plaintiff was the organizer of Tongde, etc. Compelled, on May 10th of the 18th year, the plaintiff filed a lawsuit in the civil court against Zhang Songzhou for forging the order, requesting cancellation. Datong Bank, knowing that the plaintiff had filed a lawsuit, filed another case on May 15th, claiming that the plaintiff was a shareholder of Tongde and that Ju'an was the guarantor, requesting the performance of the guarantee contract. The original claim was for 62,531 taels, but this case astonishingly ruled that the plaintiff should pay over 66,370 taels. Currently, Datong's lawsuit requesting the plaintiff to perform the guarantee contract has been suspended in the appellate court. The plaintiff's lawsuit against Zhang Songzhou for forging the order has been ordered to be prosecuted in the criminal court," etc. Yesterday, Judge Feng Shide interrogated the case in the Second Criminal Court. First, the defendant's lawyer stated, "The case is complex. The litigation has been ongoing for four years since the 16th year. The previous testimonies of both the plaintiff and the defendant are on record. However, for clarity, it is necessary to retrieve and consult the previous testimonies. Therefore, we request the court to postpone the hearing." Next, Guo Shuopeng testified, "The defendant forged twelve guarantee contracts. The strokes of the seals are different in thickness. Furthermore, the company's silver and money transactions require my signature after the seal is affixed for them to be valid. However, there are no signature traces at all." The defendant claimed, "Guo Bohan, the plaintiff's son, jointly established the Tongde Company with Lin Bangji and Lin Yingjie. Guo's son was the manager, and the plaintiff was a major shareholder. The company previously mortgaged US$200,000 of goods to the Mei Yong Petroleum Company. However, due to insufficient capital, Guo Shuopeng's sugar company acted as the guarantor. There were a total of twelve guarantee contracts. This time, in addition to the goods, the Petroleum Company also lost US$20,000, so they are seeking compensation." The plaintiff replied, "Guo Bohan is my son, but we have separated and are now living separately. I do not know where he is now." The judge then instructed that the case be adjourned for further hearing after all relevant case files are gathered.

Su Jiashan Passed Away Yesterday 198

Su Jiashan, a prominent merchant from Changshu residing in Shanghai, was highly respected for his silk business in Xichang and other places. Throughout his life, he enjoyed doing good deeds and providing financial assistance to various charitable organizations in Shanghai. He also independently established a charitable hospital in Changshu, founded a free school, and constructed roads, among other public-spirited endeavors, which were praised by his fellow villagers. Recently, he unfortunately passed away yesterday due to illness. Upon hearing the news, relatives and friends were all grieved. The funeral is scheduled for 1:00 PM tomorrow, followed by the burial at 2:00 PM.

Jingwei Company Disputes Labor Arbitration, Involved in Lawsuit 199

The Shanghai Jingwei Company in Huaxingfang, Baoding Road, previously dismissed ten workers, Xu Xilin, Yu A'ye, Shen Fei'an, Wang Zhongrui, Qian Zhangnan, Song Qiwen, Shi Hegen, He A'lin, He A'shi, and Pan Yingzhou, due to poor performance and obvious misconduct. However, Xu and the others believed that the company's dismissal was quite unreasonable. Therefore, they applied to the Shanghai Labor-Capital Arbitration Committee to summon both parties for arbitration. Subsequently, the committee ruled that Jingwei Company's dismissal of Xu Xilin and others was inappropriate and ordered reinstatement. Jingwei Company disagreed and raised an objection. On one hand, they hired lawyer Hong Shihao to submit a petition to the mediation office of the Special District Court, requesting mediation, modification of the original ruling, and rejection of the workers' demands. The reason given was that Xu and the others were originally on probation. Formal employment would only occur if the probation was satisfactory. However, after Xu and the others entered the factory, their misconduct was obvious, making dismissal unavoidable. Unexpectedly, the Labor-Capital Arbitration Committee failed to investigate and ordered reinstatement, which was unreasonable in theory and too restrictive in practice. Therefore, they legally requested mediation, modification of the original ruling. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong held a hearing for mediation. On the workers' side, lawyer Huang Xiubo attended the court. Judge Xu immediately declared that labor disputes could only be litigated after arbitration and that mediation was unnecessary. There was a ministerial order explaining this. Why was the plaintiff requesting mediation? According to lawyer Hong, Jingwei Company did not want labor and capital to reach extremes, so they requested mediation to seek a peaceful resolution. Lawyer Huang immediately stated that arbitration rulings could only be enforced by the court. Jingwei Company's request for mediation was unprecedented. Judge Xu then asked lawyer Hong for mediation opinions. The reply was that Jingwei Company intended to allow those who had not received wages to collect them at the company and then terminate the labor contract. Lawyer Huang immediately objected, saying that five of the ten workers, Xu Xilin, etc., could be expected to be reinstated. If the remaining five were not reinstated, Jingwei Company would have to pay double the wages according to the length of service. For example, if they had worked for one year, they would be paid another year's salary. Lawyer Hong indicated that he needed to seek the company's opinion and requested an extension. Lawyer Huang also agreed. Judge Xu then ordered a postponement for further review.

Minutes of the Coal Industry Association Meeting 205

The Shanghai Coal Industry Association held its 37th executive committee meeting yesterday. Agenda items: (1) How to handle the implementation of public scales and the determination of coal weight for members. It was resolved that coal stored in a yard before July 1 should still be calculated in English tons. If using metric tons, it should be calculated according to English tons. From July 1, all calculations should be based on metric tons (1 English ton = 2240 pounds, 1 metric ton = 2204.6 pounds). (2) For coal sales contracts between members and foreign firms or miners that do not specify public scales, the weight should be calculated according to English pounds. If delivered according to public scales, 35.4 pounds per ton should be added to the English pounds or deducted from the original price. (3) Members should use public scales for all coal sales and notify users accordingly. (4) Anti-opium public sale proposal. It was resolved that the secretary should draft a declaration expressing opposition. (5) How to resist the Japanese instigation of Koreans to boycott Chinese businesses. It was resolved: (1) Request the government to send warships to protect overseas Chinese. (2) Request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to make serious representations. If still ineffective, adopt a non-cooperation policy towards Japanese residing in China and order Koreans to leave.

Letter Received 210

To the Esteemed Editor-in-Chief of the Shen Bao:

Greetings. Regarding the news item "Thief Steals Guanyin" in the local news section of the fourth page of your newspaper on July 8th, it states that "Maotai Foreign Firm had a batch of Chinese antique porcelain shipped overseas for a good price." However, our firm does not engage in buying and selling imports and exports, but specializes in transshipment, customs declaration, warehousing, insurance, and also operates the Huangpu Ferry Bureau and Shanghai Handling Company. Therefore, the porcelain shipped overseas this time did not belong to our firm. Our firm only acted as a customs broker and transporter for the client. Because the information in your newspaper is slightly inaccurate, we are writing to request a correction to clarify the truth and responsibility. We earnestly pray for this. Respectfully, Maotai Foreign Firm, July 8th.

Free Talk

A Word of Wisdom 211

— Qiushui

Love, clothing, courtesy, and conversation. All were invented by women. The more women invent, the heavier the burden on men.

If there were no women in this world, there would be no vanity. We men could revert to our primitive state, using animal skins for winter and leaves for summer. We would absolutely not need clothes.

Adam and Eve. One day in the garden, they saw an apple. Adam hadn't even touched it, but Eve took it and ate it first. So sin is also something invented by women.

No young man loves to look at the moon on a spring night unless he is caught in the web of love and suffering some pain.

Those who swim well often drown. Those who are passionate often get misled by love.

The difference between an engagement ring and a wedding ring is like the difference between a promissory note and a bank draft.

An educated person is the laziest person in the world. He refuses to work and only spends his time reading.

An unmarried woman hopes she can be her fiancé's philosopher, companion, or leader. But once she gets married, she realizes she has only become his alarm clock, a food inspector, a cook, or a house servant.

A New Crime Trend Spreading from North to South 212

— Yu

Crime also has trends. For example, kidnapping for ransom is called "grabbing tickets." Previously, it rarely happened in the Jiangnan region. Since Sun Meiyao cut off the road in Lincheng and kidnapped foreigners to demand official positions, the trend of kidnapping has become prevalent. It spreads gradually from north to south and is rampant in Shanghai. This is one trend of crime. Another example is tomb raiding. Since the Eastern Mausoleums were excavated, resulting in a large collection of rare treasures, the petty thieves of Peiping have also followed suit and become a trend. Peiping originally had many noble graves, all of which were successively robbed. Even the tomb of the actor Tan Xinpei was not spared, showing how rampant it is. Now, this trend is also gradually spreading south, and will be as prevalent as the kidnapping trend. Wu County has a Song Dynasty scholar named Zhu Changwen. His tomb was also dug up and suffered the tragedy of having his remains split apart, which is heartbreaking. The matter concerns the destruction of the relics of famous scholars and has an impact on morality and people's hearts. It is different from the excavation of ordinary people's tombs. Zhu served as a proofreader in the Secretariat during the Song Dynasty. He was knowledgeable and studious. He was gentle and did not seek advancement. He built a Happy Garden in the city and read books there, which is now the old Happy Garden Academy, one of the famous sites in Wucheng. In his later years, he taught in this Prefecture and was promoted to Doctor of the Imperial Academy. He taught people to study classics first and then literature. Throughout his life, he wrote books that were either transmitted or not. The table of contents of his books is fully recorded in the History of the Song Dynasty. At the beginning of the Qing Dynasty, Emperor Qianlong allocated funds to repair the Happy Garden. Later, Jiangsu Education Commissioner Li Yinpei requested to promote famous scholars, with Zhu listed first. He was admired by later generations in this way. Unexpectedly, under the blue and white flag, his tomb was reported to have been robbed, which is regrettable. It is hoped that the authorities will arrest the main perpetrators and punish them severely to curb this evil trend of crime so that it does not spread everywhere like kidnapping.

Eagerly Entering Prison 213

— Zhou Menglin

Not Gandhi's Non-Resistance

The word "prison" is such a terrible name to us. Everyone avoids it as much as possible, so how can anyone eagerly enter it? Unexpectedly, in this world full of surprises, the people on the other side of the earth actually treat it as paradise because of the climate and geographical conditions.

It turns out that Washington State in the United States recently received a message that Point Hope, Alaska (in the northwest corner of North America), plans to bid for the construction of a larger prison than before. This was originally an ordinary matter. However, the motivation for this matter is too ridiculous. It is said that the Eskimos there not only do not feel ashamed of going to prison, but also intentionally break the law because of the harsh living conditions in the frigid zone, hoping to experience the flavor of a jail cell.

The incident occurred because not long ago, the US military arrested two natives who violated the law. This was not a rare occurrence. However, it caused a surprise. It turned out that they ate well and lived warmly in prison, which was ten times better than living in the icy and snowy conditions. So after they were released from prison, they told their companions about this haven that no one had ever discovered. As a result, they all intentionally committed crimes in order to experience the flavor of a jail cell. The prison was also declared full.

Strange Symptom of Earwigs Entering the Ear and Prevention Methods 214

— Li Xufan

Earwigs are the easiest to breed and have a long lifespan. Shanghai has a dense population, and there are even more earwigs. Although there are medicinal liquids and powders, they are not easy to popularize due to the high price. My friend Gu Zixing from Jiangsu used to live in a certain village in Zhabei. One night, after falling asleep, he was startled by something entering his ear in his sleep. He hurriedly got up and dug it out, but couldn't get it out. There was a rumbling sound in his ear. At first, he didn't know what it was. He thought it would disappear after a long time, so he didn't care. After more than ten days, he had strange pains at the upper end of the ear root and at the back of the head. The pain came and went. He tried to treat it in Shanghai without effect. After more than a month, the affected area rose up with redness and swelling. He had dizziness and tinnitus. He was mentally exhausted. He then sold his things and returned to his hometown. After being persuaded by someone, he went to Gengsheng Hospital for treatment. Dr. Hui Gengsheng diagnosed that there was a small poisonous animal lurking inside, eating blood and corroding the marrow. Surgery was required. Gu was shocked when he heard the doctor's words. Of course, he obeyed the doctor's orders. He was hospitalized overnight. The doctor performed various surgeries, cutting open from the right ear root and reaching directly to the back of the head. He found that the inner ear membrane had been broken. On the edge of the back of the head, he discovered an earwig the size of a melon seed, which was very fat. He clamped it out. It was still wriggling. The doctor said that it was fortunate that the insect was male and had not bred. If it had been female, it would have been more than two months old and would have been incurable. He gradually recovered and is still alive today. After hearing about this, I can't help but tremble during the summer months. I poured kerosene mixed with soybean oil into the cracks in my residence and bedding, which was quite effective. It is more economical than medicinal liquids and powders. I also fear that they will steal into my camp and launch a surprise attack, so I use medicinal cotton wool to plug my ears when I go to bed as a precautionary measure. Readers who have this problem, why not try it?

Cold Words 215

— Zhizheng

The South Pole is "the bottom of the world." The place is extremely cold. When Major Byrd explored it, several interesting things happened. One day, a member of the expedition team had a gap in his mask. The cold wind pierced in, and it was unbearable. He quickly removed his gloves to repair it. Little did he know that his five fingers immediately froze and could not move. Another day, a team member went out to work. After a while, he returned to the cellar, and his head and face were all silver. His whiskers and eyebrows were all white. The cold air had condensed into snowflakes. Once, an iceberg floated in the South Pole. The area was huge. If you calculated it in terms of time (it was summer in the United States at that time), if this iceberg were moved to New York, you could become a millionaire.

Travels in India (63) 216

— Spirit Flower

Everywhere, iron signs are hung. These are arranged by the Mahayana Buddhist Society. On the signs are written: "Those who damage these antiquities will be detained for three months." Occasionally there are stone tablets. On them are carved many kinds of Buddha images. The carving methods are different. The larger stone carvings often depict the Buddha's birth, renunciation, enlightenment, preaching, and nirvana. They are systematic and very impressive. Smaller carvings simply depict the Buddha's image.

There are also Westerners who come to visit. Beyond these desolate ruins, to the north, is a large river. It flows from west to east. Only in winter and spring does its water dry up, leaving only a thin stream, like a small ditch next to a vegetable garden well. One can imagine that in summer the river must be full of water. There is a bamboo forest. The bamboo leaves are very large. Men and women gather firewood, passing back and forth. The women are all dressed in red, like the Chinese depiction of Guanyin. This is because Guanyin is dressed as an Indian woman. Returning to the west side of the university, I took a short rest. I asked someone when these temples and pagodas were built, and when they were abandoned. They said they did not know. Some said they were built by King Ashoka, others said by some later king. This is because Indians do not care about history. In the past, the Mongols also said that the Mongols unified the world, but there is no history to verify this. Donations for the construction of various temples also do not list the names of donors. They laugh at the Chinese for listing names on donation plaques.

The secretary of the Buddhist Society is from Ceylon. He and a gentleman named La Hao argued about the merits of Ceylonese and Indian culture. The Ceylonese said that Ceylonese culture is superior to Indian culture, with no class distinctions, and various other advantages. The Indian, of course, did not admit that Ceylon was superior to India, and said that Chinese culture was even more ancient than Indian culture. Although I do not believe that Ceylonese culture is superior to Indian culture, I am quite surprised that the people of Ceylon are so self-confident, daring to "put dung on the Buddha's head," wanting to surpass India. Indians also do not believe that the Buddha ever went to Ceylon, but the Ceylonese say that they have the Buddha's footprints. This is quite interesting. I told the Ceylonese that they should promote Carpaater's geography book, which says that the origin of the world's people is in Ceylon, and that the Xia surname once lived there. Now there is Adam's Bridge. Based on this, they can claim to be the ancestors of all mankind. Everyone laughed and dispersed.

I returned to school again. The people I saw along the way were mostly dark-skinned. I want to study the reason why Indians are dark-skinned. Generally, half of it is related to ethnicity, and half to habits. I have seen wealthy Indian women, beautifully dressed, living with Europeans, and it is difficult to distinguish them. This is impossible for the Chinese. Poor people are mostly dark because they do not dress up and do not pay attention to hygiene. One reason is the strong sunlight. Indians consider assimilation with nature to be beautiful, and do not feel that their dark skin is bad. Another reason is that they do not wear hats and expose their heads to the sun, not knowing to cover them. However, there is a problem with wanting Indians to wear hats, because Indians like to carry things on their heads, so wearing a hat is also inconvenient. However, if one wants to be beautifully dressed, one must change and wear a hat. I have seen Indians occasionally wearing hats, but only one in a thousand.

Visiting the Chengde Factory 217

— Liang Yu

The Chengde Cotton Weaving Factory's Chen Zuolin and Zhi Fang brothers recently invited guests to visit their factory's clothing contents at the Puyi Vocational Training Center. On both sides of the hall, various flannels, woolens, silks, and crepes were displayed. Among them, the double-sided flannel and the green crepe were the best. The former is enough to compete with imported camel hair flannel, and the latter is enough to rival Indian silk. Zhao Jinqing, the Vice Minister of Industry, praised and encouraged them after seeing this. Then, factory staff led a tour of the factory. First, they entered the weaving factory. There were a total of forty-eight machines. The sound of the motors was loud, and the shuttles moved back and forth. They were weaving various bleached cloths, intending to resist foreign bleached cloths. Then, they went upstairs and entered the yarn sorting room. Thousands of threads were separated and cleaned by machines. The joining of threads was done by hand. Finally, they entered the silk weaving factory. The machines were weaving silk and Ge cloth. The various patterns were different. The difference in patterns depended entirely on the cardboard at the end of the machine. Each board had holes, arranged irregularly. The weft threads passed through, separated by the holes, and the pattern was formed. After watching for a while, they took their seats for a drink. During the banquet, the Chen brothers recounted the process of starting the factory and the harmonious relationship between labor and management. The Chengde Factory is very large in scale. The weaving machines alone total five hundred. Those in charge are divided into nine departments, named after the number of the factory. Each has its own factory site, not connected to each other. In this way, others may think that dividing up the factories would scatter the power and increase expenses. However, it is unknown that the labor unrest would be dealt with smoothly as a result. The managers actively facilitated marriages for outstanding male and female workers, providing marriage funds limited to two hundred yuan. The new couple could repay the loan monthly. Therefore, the workers were all grateful, and the business prospered. This is something that other factories should emulate. (Reward omitted)

Rotary Club Story

？？？ (16) 218

— Xu Zhuodai

"Can you write something on the cover of this book for me?"

"What is it? You're messing around again."

"Write the four characters 'Food and Sundries'."

"I don't have time!"

"You have time to eat, but after eating, you're not willing to fulfill a little obligation? This ledger is for recording the expenses of side dishes, so it is also part of the work of eating."

"Go write it yourself!"

"My handwriting is not good. I want you to write in the clerical script, it'll look better!"

"Ziliang wants me to go downstairs quickly, so the only way is to write it for her quickly." I immediately picked up the pen and wrote four characters."

"Very sloppy!"

"It's written, you can go."

"Strange! Why do you rush me away as soon as I come?"

"Don't bother me!"

"I want to ask you about a character."

"Thank you! Go downstairs!"

Ziliang was about to cry.

"I don't recognize characters, so of course I have to ask. If I don't ask you, who am I going to ask? A teacher is a teacher. I must ask you. Is the '茭' (jiao) in '茭白' (jiao bai, water bamboo shoot) the '草' (cao, grass) radical or the '竹' (zhu, bamboo) radical?"

"You don't even know that? It's the '草' (cao, grass) radical."

Mrs. was about to speak again, but Ziliang covered her ears with both hands, intending not to listen to her anymore. Suddenly, a burst of military music sounded outside. Mrs. heard it, dropped the ledger in her hand, and quickly went downstairs.

At this time, Ziliang was a little calmer, but she was very worried. She heard the military music outside and ran out to watch. The gate was of course not closed. What if the nanny also followed her? Wouldn't that be even worse than going to the back door to look at the sewer? The back door is a small alley with no through traffic, but the front door is different. What if a thief broke in and took something? What should I do?

Financial Market Speculation Resumes 219

The Impact of War Debt Extension is Still Shallow

Stock Markets in Various Countries Frequently Report Lows

This Morning's Major Forecast is Low

Cause and Effect of the Rebound 220

Yesterday, speculative gold resumed its upward trend, and the market conditions felt notably firm. However, the rise and fall were erratic, and the fluctuations were not small, making it difficult to grasp. People's minds were confused. There were twelve or thirteen changes in the morning and evening. As a result, it rose sharply by sixteen taels and zero. It rose early in the morning, because silver bars rose slightly, and the American silver market did not move. Furthermore, the international war debt extension had no impact, and stock markets in the United States and other countries were frequently low. However, the trading by various firms was very different, so the price was already hidden and lurking. Later, due to heavy purchases by major players, foreign exchange, both internal and external, became tight. The market sentiment became increasingly sharp, almost rising to seven hundred and thirty taels. However, Dalian Gang and others did not stop selling, so it fell back. The market showed sharpness again at noon. The latter market was due to the lack of drafts on Wednesday, and the initial market was flat. In the end, the situation was solid, and buyers were also strong. It is predicted that this morning's major listing will definitely be low.

Sharp Rise at the Morning Opening 221

The August opening this morning rose seven taels and one mace, calculated at seven hundred and eighteen taels. The major listing rose slightly by one-sixteenth, the silver price did not change, and there were no good or bad private telegraphs. However, there was another telegraph reporting a small one-sixteenth rise, indicating that people's minds were still good. Furthermore, Dalian Gang and Tong Taichang and others took the lead in buying, and Qian Changxiang and speculators also bought. Later, it rose to twenty-three and a half taels, with a fluctuation of one or two taels in between. Later, Fuyu and Yuanheng and others sold, so it retreated to sixteen and a half taels. Then, the English Gold Bank initially absorbed 8125, then 75. In a moment, the gold price rose again to twenty-one and a half taels. Zhifeng Yong and Wanxing and others bought in, and Yongfeng and others sold. Furthermore, the English Gold Bank's buying price of 8125, because 75 was difficult to sell, dropped again to eighteen taels and five mace. The exchange rate announcement had shrunk by 125, US dollars by 25, and Japanese gold increased by 1.5 fen, that is, twenty taels. It increased again to twenty-two and a half taels. Yiyu and others came to sell, and the English Gold still settled at 75 in September, so it was suppressed again to nineteen taels and five mace.

High Point at Twenty-Nine Taels 222

Suddenly, buying interest was strong. Daxing Yong, Qian Changxiang, Changsheng Yong, Yuanxing Yong, Yuanmao Yong, Wu, and others all bought in. Furthermore, English Gold was particularly strong, and dealers scrambled for 6875 to 625. Then the gold price jumped ten taels to twenty-nine taels at ten o'clock. Afterwards, Yuanheng, Shunli, Wanxing, and others all came to sell, and English Gold seemed to be loose, with banks dealing at 75, so the price fell sharply by ten taels again. There were two or three taels of twists and turns in between. At ten fifty, it was only nineteen taels. After eleven o'clock, it rebounded sharply. Various firms bought a lot. Hongli, Qian Changxiang, Cuichang Yong, and others all sold some. English Gold was steady and firm, and banks absorbed 75. At eleven thirty, it was about twenty-four taels. Grain and Rice Prices in the Lower Reaches of the River Rise Gradually

Shanghai North 246

A total of twenty-one or two rice boats from Changshu, Xixi, and Xianzi, etc., have arrived along the Suzhou River. The access to urban and rural areas is becoming more active. High-quality Chang rice is the main type, with fewer scattered types, so the selling price is very firm. The merchants' attitude is that during this period between harvests, the bottom inventory is weak, and they all intend to store up, so the price is very tight. However, the money is unusually tight and the prices cannot be raised too much. There is very little rice coming in. The merchants intend to buy Northern Japonica rice as the price continues to rise. Customers have little intent to buy because there is not much local rice. The price has risen one or two jiao. Five or six boats of glutinous rice have arrived, and the top quality is selling very well, with two to three hundred dan in small quantities. The situation is stable. Very little Duyang pointed rice is coming in, and the price is stable.

Shanghai South 247

Spot wheat transactions total 5,000 to 6,000 bags.

The Current State of Summer Silkworms in Yixing is Not Good 252

Continuous rain and sultry weather... Silkworm diseases are prevalent

Farmers in various towns and villages of Yixing, due to the failure of spring silkworms this year, have all started raising summer silkworms. After the silkworm eggs hatched, the weather was sunny and warm, and the development was quite smooth. Unexpectedly, when the silkworms reached the third sleep stage, there were two days and nights of heavy thunderstorms, coupled with abnormal heat, which caused the silkworms that were in a deep sleep to fail to wake up, excrete yellow and black substances, and become stiff. Deaths were reported daily. Currently, there is no market for mulberry leaves, and the silkworm harvest will inevitably be reduced.

New Summer Cocoons from Hangzhou Prefecture Enter the Market 253

Average cocoon production is only 50%... High-quality cocoons open at $55

Farmers in Linping, Gaosi, Sanbao, Nanshan, and other places in Hangzhou Prefecture have drastically increased the number of summer silkworms raised this year. However, the early silkworms suffered from the weather, and the late silkworms were not good at first. Only after the third sleep did the situation improve, and development was smoother. The new cocoons have entered the market. There are more than a dozen cocoon businesses in the entire county that have opened for business. The average cocoon production is only 50%. Businesses are competing to buy, and the supply of high-quality cocoons is not strong. Cocoon prices are expected to rise. Improved breed cocoons have opened at $55, and native breed cocoons are at $45-46.

Shuang Tonglu has been completely sold out, and Hanshan Temple opened at 9 taels and 6 qian. Sales on this street are quite good. White crepe prices remain stable, and sales are better than before, at 40-50 pieces per day. Yesterday, Tongpan was at 4 taels and 1 qian and 5 fen, Rengou at 4 taels and 1 qian and 2.5 fen, and Shuanglu at 4 taels and 1 qian.

Hardware Market: Overall Pessimistic News

French Iron Nails 257

Transactions are very few, and the market is sluggish. Standard is sold at 9 taels and 2 qian and 5 fen per barrel. Apart from sporadic small transactions, there was no news of large-scale transactions yesterday.

New Iron Wire 258

Yesterday, #16 to #20 was sold at 13 taels and 5 qian per dan, and #21 to #25 was sold at 18 taels and 7 qian and 5 fen. Transactions were very quiet, and the market outlook is not optimistic.

English Steel Plates 259

Yesterday, 7.5 li was slightly more active, sold at 6 taels and 7 qian and 5 fen, with 270-280 dan transacted. 2.5 li was slightly more active, priced at 8 taels and 7 qian and 5 fen. There was little interest in other colors.

Recorded Iron Wire Mesh 260

Over 80 boxes of "Wanzi" and "Chicken" brands were offered yesterday, with no price changes compared to before. Very few other brands were offered.

Miscellaneous News 261

7,000 boxes of tea have been shipped to England.

340 pieces of Huzhou silk have been shipped to England and France.

Over 400 pieces of rayon have been shipped from Italy.

600 pieces of pigments have been shipped from France to Shanghai.

3,800 baskets of fresh eggs have been shipped to the United States.

Ningbo News: The supply of new dried cuttlefish is booming, and the market has fallen to $31.5.

Ningbo News: The supply of various fish glues is short, and the current market has soared to $310, and merchants are scrambling to purchase.

Kobe Telegram: The production and market for Danghai Swallow products has risen by more than $10.
