Art World

The National Defense War Following the "Along the Longhai Line" 278

— Praise

Written by a company commander under Liang Zhongjia

—Wan Gu'an

Since Mr. Huang Zhenxia's war novel "Along the Longhai Line" was published in the fifth issue of "Qianfeng Monthly," it has attracted the attention of domestic authors and general readers who depict war. Naturally, most of the works in the literary world now are about love affairs and complaints, and the most popular are those that describe triangular love. These are pastimes for women on their pillows, making us feel that although the form of literature and art has undergone special changes through the New Culture Movement, the main trend of thought and general preferences are still dominated by disguised works like "The Romance of the Western Chamber," "Dream of the Red Chamber," and "Er Nu Ying Xiong." For more than a decade, the new literary world, both authors and readers, have taken pride in this, which is such a "shameful" thing.

The needs of the environment dictate that literary works can no longer allow "pastimes for women on their pillows" to dominate a generation's thoughts. In fact, there is no lack of talent capable of breaking through this environment and overthrowing these idols. However, authors who have already become famous have developed unbreakable habits in the past environment, making it difficult to abandon or change them, forming an invisible force that prevents the emergence of new forces of resistance. This is also an undeniable fact.

Works like "Along the Longhai Line," of course, cannot be considered mature in terms of technique, but they have already broken through the past literary world's bad environment and opened up a new path. This probably won't be denied. I believe that the value of literature and art lies primarily in thought, followed by technique. It is impossible to abandon thought and only talk about technique. Reading a refined and sophisticated work is far less satisfying than reading a stimulating and energetic work. Half of the reason is that the city life of scientific civilization no longer allows for the existence of the habit and interest of "half a day of idle talk and a game of chess," and the other half is the psychological reaction that arises involuntarily in the face of such a dangerous national environment.

Published at the same time as "Along the Longhai Line" was Mr. Wan Gu'an's "A Moment of Revolution." Following "Along the Longhai Line" and "A Moment of Revolution" is Mr. Wan Gu'an's

The National Defense War

This text also uses the novel genre to describe the Manzhouli Sino-Russian battle in the eighteenth year. Mr. Wan was a company commander under Liang Zhongjia of the 18th Brigade, personally experiencing the front lines and truthfully describing everything that happened. In terms of historical value, it seems to surpass "Along the Longhai Line."

Mr. Wan went south in the twentieth year to participate in military affairs along the Longhai Line. It was then that he became friends with Mr. Huang Zhenxia. This "National Defense War" was also written at the urging of Mr. Huang. The writing flows freely, without any embellishment, purely the true colors of a soldier. It is said that it will be published in the sixth issue of "Qianfeng Monthly." Now, the original preface by Mr. Huang is recorded below to show the general content.

Since the Opium War, the true face of China as a paper tiger has been exposed, and European countries have followed their 19th-century policy of political aggression, shifting from the African continent to East Asia. They have repeatedly used superior military force to oppress China. At this time, the Qing government, which ruled China, had no resistance to the outside world, and the people of the whole country were completely unaware of the vital interests of national survival. As a result, China suffered more national humiliation than any other country and fell into the humiliating position of a semi-colony. Statistics for these eighty-plus years of imperialist encroachment and annexation show that, in addition to the imperialists using political and economic aggression in the latter half of the period, the military failures involving bloodshed and sacrifice alone include the Opium War, the Anglo-French Allied Expedition, the "Ever Victorious Army" incident, the Sino-French War in Vietnam, the Eight-Nation Alliance Expedition, and the recent Guo Songling incident, the Jinan incident, and the Sino-Russian Manzhouli incident. Other incidents include the massacre on the Heilongjiang River in 1674, the failure of the Taiwanese militia, and various minor massacres and brutal oppressions, which are too numerous to record. Looking back at the war history of decades of national humiliation, we get even more shocking records.

In the Opium War, the British imperialists used 15,000 troops (mostly Indian soldiers) before and after, and the war zone expanded to Guangdong, Zhejiang, and Jiangsu provinces. The Chinese army resisted with approximately 100,000 troops or more. As a result, the British army won every battle and approached Nanjing.

In the Anglo-French Allied Expedition, the British and French imperialists used 20,000 troops before and after (half of whom were Indian and Annamese soldiers), and the war zone expanded to Guangdong and Zhili provinces. The Chinese army resisted with approximately 80,000 troops or more. In the battle of Xinhe, the British army first tested the shrapnel shells used in modern warfare. Their report to the Secretary of War at the time stated, "The results are excellent. The corpses of Tartar cavalry are all over the mountains and fields." The French army also specially created the Baliqiao Commemorative Medal to encourage "a small lesson given to the yellow race at the Yuanmingyuan." Naturally, the result of this war was that the Chinese army lost every battle, and even the capital was captured. (At that time, the British and French armies' transport teams were all Chaozhou people from Guangdong.)

The Ever Victorious Army incident was the achievement of two British and American adventurers. The adventures of Ward and Gordon. The imperialists wanted to preserve Shanghai as their future center of economic aggression, but it was inconvenient to openly interfere in China's internal unrest. Therefore, they encouraged these two adventurers to organize the Ever Victorious Army, relying on the strength of Guangdong pirates and Zhejiang rogues to defeat the attacking army of the Loyal King Li Xiucheng, creating the foundation of today's Greater Shanghai.

In the Sino-French War in Vietnam, the French imperialists used 30,000 troops before and after, and the war zone extended from Annam to Fujian and Taiwan. The Chinese army resisted with approximately 50,000 to 60,000 troops. As a result, the Chinese and French armies fought fiercely on the border between Guangxi and Annam, and the French army clearly showed signs of being unable to resist. Naval Vice Admiral Courbet also died in depression after the failed attack on Fujian. However, although China made some progress in military affairs this time, the political struggle caused an unprecedented farce, giving Annam to the enemy for nothing.

In the First Sino-Japanese War, the Japanese imperialists used approximately 70,000 to 80,000 troops, and the war zone ranged from the Yellow Sea to Shanhaiguan. The Chinese army resisted with at least 120,000 troops or more. As a result, the Chinese army lost every battle, and the Japanese army conquered China with only 4,000 casualties.

In the Eight-Nation Alliance Expedition, the total number of troops from the eight-nation alliance of Britain, France, Russia, Germany, the United States, Austria, Japan, and Italy was approximately 75,000, but only 16,000 actually participated in the fighting. The front line was only 300 li long (from Dagu to Beijing). The Chinese army resisted (including the Boxers) with a total of 300,000 troops, but the disorganized masses were of no avail, and Beijing was captured by the Allied forces.

In the Guo Songling incident, Japanese artillery joined the Feng army to assist in the attack, eliminating the revolution in the three northeastern provinces.

The Jinan incident was the May 3rd Massacre. Although the Chinese have been promoting that they were massacred without resistance, the opinion of military critics around the world only knows that the revolutionary army was defeated by the Japanese army. (A new book recently published in the United States called "Battlefield of the East" reportedly states, "Four thousand five hundred Japanese soldiers stood dangerously amidst the Chinese army's tide, which was enough to maintain the glory of their Shahe Lushun without shame." Westerners find it difficult to understand the doctrine of non-resistance on the battlefield.)

In the Sino-Russian Manzhouli incident, excluding the eastern front of Tongjiang Mishan, just looking at the battle situation in Manzhouli Zhalannuoer, the Chinese army used 15,000 troops before and after, with four artillery pieces and two airplanes. The Soviet imperialists used approximately 50,000 troops before and after, with 200 artillery pieces, 30 airplanes, and 30 tanks. As a result, although the Chinese army was defeated due to being outnumbered and outgunned, it inflicted heavy damage on the enemy.

In this series of national humiliations and war history, it goes without saying that the Sino-Russian War reveals a light of indestructible glory. After clearly explaining this blood-stained bill, let's get back to the main topic and faithfully introduce Mr. Wan Gu'an's "National Defense War." It is said that 18 li north of Manzhouli, where the Chinese Eastern Railway enters Siberia from Chinese territory, there is a wooden national gate standing precariously amidst the yellow sand and white grass, lonely expressing the sacredness of our borders. Mr. Wan used this as the theme, using a faithful pen to record all the tragic events he personally experienced, heard, and witnessed, creating this record of our country's fierce resistance to red imperialism.

The entire article is approximately 60,000 characters long. The author is a company commander under Liang Zhongjia of the 15th Brigade, who fought the fiercest in this battle. With the warm blood of a native of Guanwai and the forthright character of a soldier, he straightforwardly wrote down his various impressions, filled with patriotism everywhere, flowing out from the heart without the slightest hypocrisy. Among them, the actual life of soldiers, the brutality of the Red Guards, the tension during shelling, and the tragic sacrifices during the final breakout are not only unprecedented descriptions in our country's literary world, but also a rare work in various Asian countries besides Japan.

Looking back at the works in the literary world that describe war in recent years, such as Sun Xizhen's "On the Battlefield" and Ms. Bing Xin's "War Diary," although they also have their considerable merits, "National Defense War" still occupies the first place for creative works using foreign wars as the subject matter. The advantage of "National Defense War," excluding the author's technique, is its "authenticity" because the facts all come from the author's personal experience, and it can also be said to be part of his life history, a "heroic diary."

At that time, Mr. Wan also married a Russian girl, but he did not expect that she was an enemy spy. In the "Spy" chapter of this book, the author puts his patriotic heart above all else and resolutely kills his lover. "In short, she was for her country, and I was for my country." For this reason, his beloved wife, Liubo, went to become a ghost in the "Tomb of Red Heroes," and he also fought to the bitter end in the trenches of the lonely city under the setting sun, breaking out of the encirclement amidst the smoke and bullets with a heart full of enthusiasm, sadly watching the enemy's sickle and axe replace the flagpoles of Manzhouli.

After reading "National Defense War," I couldn't help but come to a realization. In the past, the Chinese people had a kind of contempt for their own army, thinking that the result of the Chinese army fighting the enemy must be a disastrous defeat. This is also a clear proof given to us by the history of national humiliation. However, readers only need to take a look at "National Defense War," take a look at those warriors who used unusable machine guns to resist the charge of thousands of enemy cavalry, and take a look at those hundreds of heroes who fought tanks with their bare hands and flesh. Chinese people, believe in the military power of your motherland!

The Greeks have the three hundred warriors in the Thermopylae Pass, the Japanese have the Yamato spirit under Lushun Mountain, the Turks have Osman Pasha of Plevna, the French have the guards who died unyielding at Waterloo, the British have the light cavalry of Balaclava, and we also have our heroes in the snowy Manzhouli.

People hiding in Guanli, people in the big cities with their red lanterns and green wine, people complaining in the pavilions, young people of China, do you still remember that incident on November 21, 1929? Do you still remember that six thousand miles away, under the national gate of yellow sand and white grass or icy snow, there were thousands of brave and tragic northeastern men resisting the red terror? I am afraid you have completely forgotten it. If you have forgotten, please look at—"National Defense War"—

In short, the above are just some scattered introductions. In the future, when people share the same vision, someone will naturally come out to take on the responsibility of criticism. Because I had previously strongly encouraged Mr. Wan in Henan to write his spoken stories into articles, now that he has successfully completed them and written them more vividly and powerfully than he narrated, I am of course very happy to write this short introduction.

Social News

More People Read Books in American Libraries 282

The Unemployed Seek Inexpensive Education; Book Content Shifts From the Fictitious to the Real

According to American newspapers, during this economic downturn, the number of people reading books in libraries has increased significantly, and the types of books selected have also shifted from novels to more practical works, such as history, travel, biographies, languages, and industrial guidance. The reason is that unemployed people have nothing to do and often go to libraries to read and pass the time, and seek inexpensive education. At the same time, the publishing industry is also showing the same trend. According to the latest survey, the most novels were published in 1927, totaling 36 million copies. Only 6 million copies were published in 1929. The publication of history books alone has increased significantly, totaling 3 million volumes. Some people say that writers have recently been striving for simpler texts and are increasingly inclined to the interest of human affairs, so the number of readers is increasing.

Japanese Car Industry Asks for Rewards for Exports to China 283

More Than 100 Vehicles Have Been Accepted; 500 Vehicles Are Under Negotiation

According to the Dongbao, the Japanese Vehicle Company is working hard to sell to China Railways because the domestic market is poor. Recently, the Automobile Manufacturing Company, Kawasaki Vehicle Company, and Japanese Vehicle Company have jointly accepted an order for 100 freight cars and 4 locomotives for the Jiaoji Railway, manufactured by the South Manchuria Railway's Shahe Factory. Due to the long-term impact of the war, China's railways have been somewhat abandoned. In order to improve them, they are successively ordering newly built vehicles from the Japanese Vehicle Company. The current issues are as follows:

Shenhai Railway: 30 passenger cars

Longhai Railway: 6 locomotives

Ditto: 200 freight cars

Jinpu Railway: 80 locomotives

Jiaoji Railway: Ditto 10

Ditto: 200 freight cars

However, according to China's financial situation, it is difficult to pay immediately. It is proposed to pay in installments within three years after delivery. The Shanghai Bank of China was asked to guarantee the amount, but the bank refused. The Japanese car industry is currently appealing to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Finance, asking them to use the surplus of more than 1.6 million yuan from the special accounting for Sino-Japanese cultural affairs to ensure the recovery of the price of vehicle exports, etc.

European Conference on Rural Health Opens 284

Three Proposals

Geneva News: The European Conference on Rural Health initiated by the League of Nations, prepared by the Preparatory Committee of this conference and the Small Committee of Experts on Rural Health Improvement, opened on June 29. The conference will last until July 11. The proposals are as follows: (1) The principle of maintaining effective medical assistance in rural areas; (2) The most effective method for organizing health affairs in rural areas; (3) Effective and most economical methods for rural health improvement.

French General Foch's European War Diary 285

— Translated by Gu Angruo

Twenty-eighth. The enemy occupied the high ground south of the Vansel River and stopped advancing. (Note: The reason for the stoppage was later discovered to be as follows: The German army attacked the British army from March 21 to April 9. At first, it was quite successful, but due to the assistance of the French reserve forces, it eventually failed. The enemy then decided to continue attacking the British army in front of the French front, first restricting the French reserve forces, so there was the attack on the Ximing River on May 27. The original plan of the Ximing River attack was only to occupy the high ground south of the Vansel River as the goal. This is the reason why the enemy stopped advancing on the 28th. Seeing the unexpected victory within two days, the German high command changed its plan that night and ordered the attack to continue, attacking southwestward past Sayasson, directly heading for Paris, and attacking southward to take the Marne River, cutting off the Paris-Nancy railway.) Twenty-ninth. The attack resumed, more violently than the previous two days. The French army has been severely damaged and is unable to resist. The enemy's central front is 15 to 20 miles long and is advancing rapidly, occupying the high ground controlling the north bank of the Marne River that evening.
